Local News

Shanghai Business Association and Over Two Hundred Other Public Groups Held a Farewell Reception for Weng Zhaoyuan Yesterday 142

Mr. Weng Offered "Saving the Nation Through Aviation" as a Parting Message

Various Public Groups Telegraphed the Philippine Chinese Chamber of Commerce to Request a Welcome

General Weng Zhaoyuan, Brigade Commander of the 156th Brigade of the 78th Division of the 19th Route Army, has decided to set sail today on the American liner President Madison. Mr. Weng boarded the ship at 9:00 PM last night. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, over two hundred public groups in the city held a farewell reception at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, attended by hundreds of people from all walks of life in the city, including Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, and Wen Hongen. Mr. Yu, Mr. Wang, and others delivered farewell speeches. The details are recorded as follows:

Attendees: There were many attendees yesterday, reaching over three hundred people, including Yu Qiaqing, Wen Lanting, Wang Yansong, and Wang Xiaolai from the Shanghai business community; Lin Kanghou from the banking sector; Wen Hongen, the Chief of the Public Security Bureau; Yin Zhiling from various national salvation associations; Wu Mai from the National Lawyers Association; Zhou Xuexiang, Chen Peide, and Chen Yafu from the General Labor Union; Wang Zhaocheng from the Citizens' Federation; Pei Yunqing from the Money Trade Association; Guo Shun from the Municipal Council, and General Weng Zhaoyuan. General Weng Zhaoyuan arrived at the venue at 3:00 PM, and the meeting commenced immediately, with Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Wen Lanting, Zhang Yichen, Zhang Zilian, Li Yongxiang, and Wang Zhaocheng serving as the presidium.

Meeting Agenda: (1) Ringing the bell to begin the meeting; (2) Publicly electing the presidium; (3) The chairperson reporting the purpose of the meeting; (4) The chairperson reading the farewell address; (5) General Weng delivering a speech; (6) Taking a photograph; (7) Entertainment, Scout performance; (8) Playing military music; (9) Completion of the ceremony and adjournment.

Chairperson's Report: After the ceremonial procedures, the chairperson Wang Xiaolai first reported, saying, "Today, various groups in Shanghai are holding this meeting to bid farewell to Brigade Commander Weng as he goes abroad. This is truly because of Brigade Commander Weng's great achievements during the January 28th Shanghai Incident, which had a life-and-death relationship with our people. The reason for Brigade Commander Weng's trip abroad is, on the one hand, to represent the 19th Route Army in thanking the overseas Chinese in Nanyang for their enthusiastic assistance during the Shanghai Incident, and on the other hand, because Mr. Weng deeply understands that in modern warfare, air power is as important as naval and land forces. He resolutely goes abroad to study the aviation industries of various countries in order to implement the principle of saving the nation through aviation. We are moved by the greatness of Mr. Weng's trip abroad, and therefore hold this meeting to bid him farewell. When Brigade Commander Weng was bravely defending Wusong, he fell from an airplane three times but remained safe. This shows that Brigade Commander Weng's patriotism is sincere and moves the heavens."

Portrait of General Weng Zhaoyuan

Farewell Address: Next, Wang Yansong, representing the farewell group, delivered a farewell address, saying, "Our beloved General Weng Zhaoyuan will, in November of the 21st year of the Republic of China, be entrusted by the 19th Route Army and the Chinese Aviation Construction Association to go abroad and convey their mission. The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and over a hundred other public groups are therefore bidding him farewell, shedding tears of sorrow, expressing fervent hopes, and writing words of utmost affection as a gift, wishing that the General would accept and cherish them with sincerity. Since the invasion of the violent bandits, our Northeast has been occupied for more than a year. During this period of over a year, although the national crisis remains profound, our national strength to resist the enemy has become clear. Those who are rampaging and killing in the Northeast today are all the enemy's elite. We are defending against them with righteous people who lack both weapons and ammunition, yet we have already made them weary and running for their lives. During the January 28th Incident, when tens of thousands of enemy troops wreaked havoc in Shanghai, we relied on troops who regarded death as their return and forced them to retreat. Not only that, but when the General was defending Wusong, the forts were destroyed, and all defenses were exhausted. What he relied on to fight the enemy were only the blood and flesh of five hundred elite soldiers. The enemy ships that surrounded and attacked, and the airplanes that bombed, were all unable to use their violence to the fullest extent. Moreover, as the General retreated, they knew what to fear and dared not pursue him relentlessly. If we had the same weapons as them, the enemy would surely collapse at the mere sight of us. Now, the General is about to depart. We hope that he will fulfill his mission, exert his utmost efforts, and sincerely express our gratitude to the overseas Chinese, and rely on the strength of the overseas Chinese to complete the construction of aviation, internally to restore our national territory and protect our nation, and externally to alert the international community and awaken them from their dreams. The current international situation has gradually fallen into a state of injustice. This is not because the international community is truly without justice, but because it fears the strong and seeks temporary peace, sacrificing treaties in order to protect itself. Is this the way to seek wholeness? It is to destroy oneself by destroying others. Tracing the history of the world and examining its records, no country has not progressed from tribal warfare to the realm of the rule of law. The reason for creating the rule of law is to use its power to stop the cycle of killing and prevent the people of the same country from being sacrificed again. The intention of former US President Wilson in initiating the League of Nations, the establishment of the League, and the covenant jointly observed by its members, was also to eliminate the endless cycle of tribal warfare between nations and lead the world into the realm of the rule of law, so that the people of the world could enjoy peace and no longer be sacrificed in the killing between two countries. His plan was extremely benevolent and his vision was extremely compassionate. Now, this foundation of benevolence and compassion has been attacked by violence, and the member states that have the responsibility to protect the foundation of benevolence and compassion are actually threatened by violence and do not rise up to seek legitimate resistance, but sit idly by and watch the expansion of the scope of killing in order to seek unattainable security. This is truly the utmost folly in the world and the misfortune of mankind. Today, the economic panic in the world and the phenomenon of unemployment in various countries are known to everyone as the result of the losses and casualties of the European War. The lessons of the past are clear, yet they still do not awaken themselves and say that they are not in a dream. This is what the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and over a hundred other public groups hope that the General's trip will awaken the international community from its dreams. If the international community cannot be awakened from its dreams, then our entire nation, both military and civilians, will have to gather economic strength and prepare the spirit of sacrifice to await the General's return, so that the national strength that is sufficient to resist the enemy today can use the authority of the air to impose legitimate sanctions on the violence that undermines the treaties, thereby restoring our national territory, protecting our nation, and adding to the historical record of the world's protection of the law. Therefore, the General's trip is not only for the nation but also for the peace of the world. The General is about to depart, and he will surely not fail to live up to the expectations of the entire nation, both military and civilians. Respectfully presented."

Mr. Weng's Speech: "Chairperson, fellow compatriots, I am truly unworthy of today's farewell from everyone. This time, I am going abroad on behalf of the 19th Route Army and the Aviation Association to study the aviation industries of various countries and to thank the overseas Chinese in Nanyang. I have already resigned from my military post, so I am no longer a national official but only a Chinese soldier. I have resigned from my military post this time to promote the aviation industry with all my strength. All of our people also deeply understand that China cannot be saved without aviation. Dr. Sun Yat-sen's teachings also include the instruction to save the nation through aviation. After the January 28th Shanghai Incident, the people of the country should feel the necessity of promoting aviation even more. I believe that everyone has this feeling and holds this hope. Aviation has its important significance in national defense. When the Japanese army invaded Shanghai this spring, in addition to the army, there were also more than ten warships. When they besieged the Wusong forts, although the artillery fire was fierce, our army fought calmly and ultimately did not lose an inch of our land. Our greatest loss was the lack of air defense equipment. The warships used by the violent Japanese to invade us cost over 30 million yuan each to build and took more than ten years to complete, and their effectiveness was only for destruction. Other countries need a large naval force to protect their overseas territories and to demonstrate their power to their colonies. This is the weapon needed by imperialists. Our country does not have a fully equipped shipyard and lacks skilled technicians, so promoting aviation to strengthen national defense is necessary. I hope that all of my compatriots will enthusiastically promote it. I take this opportunity to wish everyone good health and thank you for your kindness."

Representative Speeches: After Mr. Weng finished his speech, Mr. Yu Qiaqing and Mr. Lin Kanghou gave speeches in succession. Mr. Yu briefly said, "Today, various circles are bidding farewell to General Weng. I believe that everyone is deeply aware of General Weng's deeds and there is no need to elaborate. General Weng raised the dignity of the Chinese people in the Wusong campaign. In the past, various countries had contempt for our army, but General Weng was able to hold out for more than thirty days under the combined attacks of Japanese warships and airplanes. The people of various countries should change their attitude and not despise our army. In addition to studying the army, General Weng is also interested in aviation. He has been in a plane crash three times and has not been injured. This is heaven helping our General Weng. General Weng has resigned from his post this time to go abroad to study aviation and to inspect the air forces of various countries. After returning to China, he will establish an aircraft factory and organize civil aviation."

(Photo by Xu Tianzhang): Group photo at the farewell reception for General Weng Zhaoyuan.

"His return is expected to be after August, at which time we will hold another meeting to welcome him," Mr. Yu said. Mr. Lin Kanghou briefly said, "During the anti-Japanese war in Shanghai, I heard of General Weng's name and admired him privately. A few days ago, I met General Weng at a banquet and had a brief conversation, and it was as if we were old friends. I admired him so much on a normal basis that it felt like we were old friends at our first meeting. General Weng has always advocated that the Chinese people cooperate and help each other to unite against the enemy, and he is also known for his integrity, adherence to the law, and responsibility. If our soldiers could all be like General Weng, then the neighboring countries' prying would not be so fearful."

Presentation of Commemorative Badge: After the speeches, the chairperson Wang Xiaolai, on behalf of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and other groups, presented a commemorative badge. The badge was a silver wreath with gold stars and open wings cast on it, which was very beautiful. Amidst the applause of the entire venue, Mr. Wang personally pinned it on General Weng's left lapel. After the presentation of the badge, General Weng thanked everyone and briefly said, "I am very grateful for the commemorative badge presented by various groups. In the future, if I encounter difficulties abroad, seeing this commemorative badge will be like seeing everyone, and I will be even more courageous to deal with everything."

Telegram to Overseas Chinese: Yesterday, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce and three other groups sent a telegram to the Philippine Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, requesting that they welcome General Weng Zhaoyuan upon his arrival. The telegram read, "To the esteemed Philippine Chinese General Chamber of Commerce, Mr. Weng Zhaoyuan has been ordered to go to various ports overseas to thank the overseas Chinese. He will depart on the President Madison of the Dai Lai Steamship Line and head to the Philippines. Please welcome him upon his arrival. Sincerely, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Guangzhao Public Association, and the Chaozhou Shanghai Association."

Boarding the Ship Last Night: After the meeting adjourned yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai Local Association hosted a banquet in the evening to welcome Mr. Weng Zhaoyuan, who was scheduled to board the President Madison at 9:00 PM. The ship will set sail this morning.

France Has Yet to Fulfill the Sino-French Treaty Signed Two Years Ago 143

Old Treaty Abolished, New Treaty Not Implemented: Overseas Chinese Like Nationals Without a Treaty

Hundreds of Thousands of Overseas Chinese in Danger of Economic Instability

丨Saigon Chamber of Commerce Sends Representatives Back to the Country to Petition丨

The Guowen News Agency reports that since the establishment of the National Government, in view of the unequal treaties between China and the world, it began in the 17th year of the Republic to respectively notify the envoys of various countries stationed in China to negotiate and sign equal treaties in order to facilitate the development of commerce between the two countries and to strengthen diplomatic relations. So far, treaties have been signed with more than a dozen countries. Unexpectedly, the new treaty signed by the Minister of Foreign Affairs of our country and the French Plenipotentiary Minister to China on May 16, 19th year of the Republic, was promulgated by our country long ago, but the French government has not yet ratified it, so that hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese in French-controlled territories are in a position of being nationals without a treaty everywhere. Commerce is almost stagnant, and the economy is in danger of being without a firm foothold. The Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Saigon, Vietnam, resolved in a general meeting to send its legal counsel, Huang An, and its former secretary-general, Xu Yixian, back to the country to petition the central ministries and departments and negotiate with the French government to ratify and implement the new treaty as soon as possible, and to ask the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to implement it separately in accordance with the spirit of the new treaty, in order to save the crisis of the overseas Chinese. The following is a record of the talks between Huang and Xu and the official letter of the Chinese General Chamber of Commerce in Saigon, Vietnam:

Letter from the Saigon Chamber of Commerce to Lin Kanghou: Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, yesterday received Huang An and Xu Yixian, who returned from Vietnam. A letter from the Saigon Chamber of Commerce is enclosed. The original letter reads: "Dear Sirs, overseas Chinese merchants have been doing business in Vietnam for a long time, and there has always been a commercial treaty to protect them. Since the resident government announced and implemented the new customs tariff in the 18th year of the Republic, at the same time, all Sino-French new commercial treaties regarding Vietnam have not been implemented. During the past period when the old treaty was abolished and the new treaty was not implemented, the overseas Chinese merchants in Vietnam were in the position of people of a country without a treaty. According to international precedents, imported goods from countries without treaties are taxed according to ordinary tariffs. When the old Vietnamese treaty was still in effect, our goods received special tariff preferences. In recent years, they have been treated with ordinary tariffs, and the tax has increased by ten to several tens of percent. Overseas Chinese merchants bear heavy taxes, and business is extremely difficult. Moreover, Vietnam is shrouded in economic depression, and the commercial arena is becoming increasingly sluggish. Overseas Chinese have failed and lack the means to maintain themselves. In addition, in August of this year, the Vietnamese-Japanese commercial treaty was announced and implemented. According to this treaty, Japanese goods, such as tea, silk, porcelain, and paper, are subject to the most-favored-nation tariff treatment. Other goods are also reduced by 10% to 60% according to ordinary tariffs. On the other hand, our goods are taxed according to ordinary tariffs. As a result, the cost of our goods and Japanese goods is very different, and it is even more difficult to sell our goods. Chinese merchants are in a desperate situation. If this continues, Chinese will not be able to gain a foothold in Vietnam. In view of this, our chamber of commerce decided at this month's regular meeting to send Mr. Huang An, the consultant, to Beijing to submit a document to the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee, urging the implementation of the Vietnamese commercial treaty, and to meet with the authorities in the name of representatives to explain in detail the various sufferings of the overseas Chinese, etc., as recorded in the case. Naturally, the case will be executed as it stands, and Mr. Huang An will be sent back to the country in mid-month to petition. I am afraid that it will be difficult to clap with one hand, and I have to seek help from others. I have always admired your association for its position as a joint organization of merchant institutions, and for taking the interests of merchants as its primary duty. Although overseas Chinese merchants are far away from the motherland, they are closely related to the motherland's commerce and all economic phenomena. Accordingly, I have recorded the plight of overseas Chinese merchants and the whole story of sending personnel to request the implementation of the Vietnamese commercial treaty and sent it to your association. I sincerely ask you to petition the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to urge the Chinese and French governments to implement the Vietnamese commercial treaty signed in May of the 19th year of the Republic, and to ask your association to provide other appropriate assistance, so that overseas Chinese merchants can slightly reduce the pain of heavy tariffs. As for all the methods and processes of carrying out assistance, I hope to see a reply. I am extremely eager to do so. Sincerely yours,

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Assists in the Process: The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce believes that this case is related to the livelihoods of overseas Chinese and has a great impact on the export of domestic goods. Yesterday morning, Chairman Lin specially sent Secretary Gu Huaibing and Clerk Ge Tianhao to visit the two representatives, Huang and Xu, at their residence to discuss the methods of implementation. They returned to the association after about an hour. It is reported that Huang and Xu are scheduled to go to Beijing this week to petition the central government. In addition to preparing a petition, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce will also provide strong assistance.

Two Representatives Talk About the Content of the Treaty: A reporter from the Guowen News Agency, introduced by Chairman Lin of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, visited the two representatives, Huang and Xu, at their residence to talk about the content of the Sino-French treaty and the current situation of the overseas Chinese. The main points are excerpted as follows: The two representatives said: (1) The treaty signed by our Minister of Foreign Affairs and the French Plenipotentiary Minister to China on May 16 of the 19th year of the Republic stated in the first article that all previous old treaties between China and France, such as the Tianjin Land Trade Treaty of the 12th year of Guangxu, the Beijing Commercial Special Treaty of the 13th year of Guangxu, and the Commercial Supplementary Articles of the 21st year of Guangxu, were all abolished. (2) Article 3 of the new treaty stipulates that the Chinese government may station consuls in Hanoi, Haiphong, and Saigon in Vietnam, and the French government may continue to station consuls in the locations listed in the previous treaty (Guangxi's 　Zhou, Yunnan's Simao, Hekou, Mengzi). (3) Article 5 of the same treaty and its annex (2) A and B have signed the following: Chinese people in Vietnam and French people in the above-mentioned locations shall have the right to reside, travel, and engage in industry and commerce. The treatment given to these people to exercise these rights in accordance with the current regulations and laws of Vietnam or China shall not be inferior to the treatment enjoyed by the people of any other country. The donations and other taxes paid by Chinese people in Vietnam and French people in the ten Chinese locations shall not be different from or higher than those paid by the people of the most-favored-nation country. (4) Annex to the same treaty, (4) Item A, regarding Article 5 of the Sino-French Special Treaty signed today, I, the ambassador, would like to reiterate to your minister that the government of this country does not consider the provisions contained in this treaty as preventing it from collecting from the Chinese people, the relevant taxes related to the exercise of special rights historically enjoyed in Vietnam, etc. According to the above articles, we can first make the following simple conclusions: (A) From the date of abolition of all old treaties to the end of October of this year, a total of two years and five months, during this period, the old treaty has become ineffective, and the new treaty has not been implemented. Hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese in Vietnam have become people of a country without a treaty. (B) Since the new treaty has not been implemented, the consuls are obviously absent, so for the past two or three years, all negotiations have been at a standstill. Even the consular visa manifest regulations promulgated by our government recently cannot be implemented. The overseas Chinese in Vietnam do not know what to do. Some of them ask the chamber of commerce for proof, while others ask the guild hall to help issue visas. The foreign merchants there are even more confused. There is no legitimate organization to give them a proper explanation. Moreover, they have witnessed that the visa issuing organization lacks the professional qualifications for visa issuance and allows cargo merchants to choose freely, so they laugh and ridicule it as child's play. (C) Since the old treaty has become ineffective, all rights in the old treaty have been cancelled. Although the new treaty has not been implemented, all obligations in the new treaty must be borne. For example, (A) Regarding tariffs, in the era of the old treaty (that is, three years ago), all goods shipped from our country to Vietnam either paid special taxes (that is, special light taxes, which only applied to Chinese people, because the goods came from China, and most of them were purchased by overseas Chinese, which did not conflict with the development of French and Vietnamese industry and commerce, and had special characteristics, hence the name special tax) or paid reciprocal taxes, but ordinary tariffs. Since the old treaty was declared invalid, all Chinese goods have not only been unable to enjoy the first type of special light tax, but also the second type of ordinary reciprocal tax has also been completely cancelled. All goods are subject to the third type of the highest tariff rate for countries without treaties. The difference between the old tax and the new tax is from two or three times to eight or nine times or dozens of times. Therefore, the promotion of domestic goods has gradually come to an end from a standstill. (B) Regarding miscellaneous taxes

Page 14

In addition to paying business tax, land tax, and residence tax, overseas Chinese in Vietnam must also pay surcharges. This type of surcharge is a necessary tax for Chinese people and is not generally applied to overseas Chinese from other countries in Vietnam. The surcharge rate is directly proportional to business, land, and other taxes, and is about twice as high. For example, if the business tax or land tax is 1,000 yuan, an additional 1,200 yuan must be paid, for a total of 2,200 yuan. According to the laws of the resident government, all regular taxes or surcharges should be paid before April of each year. If they are not paid by the deadline, the government will seal the business and auction it. If the residence tax is owed, they will be expelled from the country. (C) According to Article 5 of the new treaty, the rights and treatment of Chinese legal persons in China or overseas Chinese in Vietnam shall not be inferior to the treatment enjoyed by the people of any other country, and the donations or other taxes they pay shall not be different from or higher than those paid by the people of the most-favored-nation country. This kind of clear text is only for consolation on paper and is greatly contrary to the facts. There is no need to prove it. Even taking a step back, the French Plenipotentiary Minister to China informed our Minister of Foreign Affairs on the date of signing the new treaty (Annex 3A) that the government of this country (France) does not consider the provisions contained in that article as preventing it from collecting from the Chinese people the relevant taxes related to the exercise of special rights historically enjoyed in Vietnam, etc. It means that overseas Chinese in Vietnam have historically enjoyed special rights and should continue to pay the special taxes that have been paid historically. May I ask what the other party means by special rights? Is it the special light tax on the population of Chinese goods, or do Chinese people have the right to own property, bid, and navigate inland rivers? Let me give a more detailed explanation. (1) The special light tax enjoyed by Chinese goods imported in the past has now become a special heavy tax. (2) Not only do Chinese people have the right to own property, but also any national in Saigon (that is, the general name of Saigon, Chidi, and the suburbs, which the French call the colony) has the right to own property. If it is said that in the area of Tokyo and Phnom Penh (which the French call the protectorate, Chinese people also have the right to own property, then only overseas Chinese in Tokyo and Phnom Penh pay surcharges. Why do overseas Chinese in Saigon suffer for no reason? (3) Bidding (referring to contracting public projects, etc.) and inland river navigation, because the Annamese people are not accustomed to this kind of business, and the French are unwilling to do it. In fact, the Chinese people's contribution to the large and small buildings in Vietnam and the communication of inland river transportation is so important to the development of local industry and commerce. We are unwilling to take credit for ourselves, but why do the French reluctantly regard it as a special right of overseas Chinese? If so, it is not difficult for the operators among the overseas Chinese to unload the burden and let the Annamese people do it themselves or the French do it for them. In recent years, business has been bleak, and the market has been depressed. Contracting and shipping have been losing money and have been in a slump. All kinds of rights that the other party said were specially enjoyed by overseas Chinese have been completely eliminated due to changes in local laws or changes in the natural environment, and the heavy taxes added because of the rights still exist. Overseas Chinese lack treaty protection and lack the clever strategy of turning things into gold, then the crisis in the future will be unbearable to speak of. Overseas Chinese will never sit idly by and wait for death. Therefore, the Saigon General Chamber of Commerce, through a general meeting, specially sent my brothers and others back to the country to appeal to the National Government's Executive Yuan, Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee, and on behalf of hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese in Vietnam, made the following requests: (1) Please ask the National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs to urge the French government to fulfill the treaty signed by the French Plenipotentiary Minister to China in Nanjing on May 16, 1930, as soon as possible. (2) Please ask our government to implement the important points in the treaty: (A) Send consuls to protect them and foster good relations. (B) Negotiate to cancel the harsh taxes that have lost their basis in order to relieve the suffering of the overseas Chinese. The above few articles are only the most obvious ones. Other issues, such as the need to improve the treatment of overseas Chinese in the Saigon Immigration Bureau, the trouble of import and export procedures, the entanglement of overseas Chinese in lawsuits in the courts, and other issues, are all about having a consul first, and then negotiating separately. Overseas Chinese are hoping for the implementation of the new treaty, like hoping for clouds and rain in a long drought. If the new treaty is not implemented for a long time, the life of the overseas Chinese will be withered and dried up, and will disappear from dryness. If the new treaty is not implemented, not only will there be no consuls to negotiate for the overseas Chinese, but when will the population tariff, which is as heavy as carrying a mountain, be reduced? It should be noted that hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese buy domestic goods worth more than tens of millions of yuan a year and are the only customers for selling domestic goods. Even if the overseas Chinese themselves are not worth regretting, shouldn't our country find a way out for the budding industry? In May of this year, the French government and Japan newly concluded the Vietnam Commercial Treaty, which was announced and implemented in August. Tea, porcelain, silk fabrics, paper, etc. from Japan to Vietnam are given the most-favored-nation tariff treatment, and some Japanese goods are specially reduced in tax by 10% to 60%. If this continues, overseas Chinese will not only be unable to be direct customers of domestic goods, but will also inevitably become consumers of enemy goods indirectly. How can the pain be expressed? Although overseas Chinese are far away in foreign lands and live under the eaves of others, they never forget their concern for the motherland. When they get good news from the country, they tell each other and forget to sleep and eat. On the contrary, they are worried and all try their best to remedy the situation together. The donations to natural disasters and man-made disasters in various provinces of our country, the reward for past charitable causes, and the diligence in purchasing various public bonds are all about saving money and food and jointly relieving the country's difficulties. Overseas Chinese love their country and are not behind others, so the government's policy of protecting them should especially inherit the late Premier's legacy of supporting overseas Chinese and provide relief as soon as possible, so as to avoid hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese in Vietnam from falling into an unmanageable situation. Then our country's diplomacy is fortunate, and the survival of the future of the overseas Chinese is fortunate, etc.

The Anti-Civil War Alliance abolished and reorganized. Military Commission Yan, Halberd Seal.

The National Federation of All Circles for National Salvation Closed Yesterday 147

The National Federation of All Circles for National Salvation convened an inaugural meeting on the 30th. It was originally planned to close the meeting the day before yesterday (31st), but because the conference work was numerous and needed to be discussed urgently, the session was extended until yesterday morning (1st) before it was closed.

Closing Ceremony: At 9:00 a.m. yesterday, the representatives Xie Naishi, Long Xiangsan, Zhang Zhiyuan, Cai Chongli, Liu Chuanzhong, Dong Mosheng, Chen Zhenquan, etc. arrived one after another and began the closing ceremony. The procedure was: (1) Music, (2) Paying the highest respect to the Party and the National Flag and the portrait of the Premier, (3) Silent tribute to the compatriots who died in the Northeast, (4) The Chairman respectfully reads the Premier's will, (5) Passing the conference declaration, (6) The Presidium reads the congratulatory telegrams from various places (13 items), (7) Report by the Volunteer Army Representative, (8) Closing address, (9) Music and closing, and shouting slogans.

Volunteer Army Report: After the conference declaration was passed, the Presidium read 18 congratulatory telegrams from all parties (omitted). After reading, Yang Yijie, the representative of Geng Jizhou, the commander of the 4th Route of the Volunteer Army in western Liaoning, was invited to the conference to report on the anti-Japanese situation of the Volunteer Army, saying, "Representatives, today I am very honored to be invited by the conference to meet you here. The enthusiasm of all comrades for resisting Japan and saving the country is even more admirable to me. I have already given a brief report on the battle situation of the Volunteer Army in western Liaoning at the preparatory meeting of your association. Today, I might as well explain it to you in detail again. There are now a lot of volunteer armies in the Northeast. Even the 4th Route Army alone has more than 30,000 people. Most of these people are local people. Under the brutal oppression and massacre of Japanese imperialism, no one is not indignant and joins the volunteer army to fight to the death with the Japanese army. Therefore, although Japanese imperialism has sharp guns and cannons, it is finally no match for the determined volunteer army. Since the fall of Jinzhou, the news between the volunteer army outside the customs and inside the customs has unfortunately been cut off, so the various places inside the customs cannot know the detailed news of the volunteer army. The volunteer army outside the customs, which is really fighting hard in a bloody battle, not only does not receive substantial assistance from the government, but also does not receive sufficient relief from the compatriots. The salary and weapons are all cut off. They have to fight desperately in the cold and artillery fire on an empty stomach and wearing single clothes. This is really the most painful thing. Therefore, I sincerely hope that the representatives attending the meeting today can unite together and strive for the country and the nation to be the backing of our volunteer army. Then we will be willing to die of hunger and in battle. Finally, I have one more thing to report to you, that is, what the volunteer army needs now is food and military equipment, not money. Fellow compatriots from all walks of life, rather than taking out money to donate to the volunteer army, I am afraid that it will be embezzled by people, it is better to really take out money to buy airplanes, guns, cannons, food and supplies and give them directly to the volunteer army.

Closing Address: After the volunteer army representative finished his report, Zhang Junguang of the Presidium gave a closing address, saying, "Representatives, our conference was originally scheduled to close in two days, but because there was so much work, it was extended to today before it closed. After two and a half days of enthusiastic discussion, we have finally achieved a very satisfactory result. At this conference, all the representatives were able to fully express their opinions with their own unique insights and established so many resolutions. If these many resolutions can be implemented in a real and thorough manner, then we believe that China's anti-Japanese movement will definitely have new development. Therefore, I hope that after the closing of the meeting, all the representatives will work together to implement the resolutions of the conference, so that these many resolutions will not become empty talk on paper and complete our great mission and thoroughly eliminate the shackles of imperialism. At the closing of this meeting, I have no better ideas to offer to the representatives, only my sincere hope, celebrating the bright and victorious future."

Yesterday Morning, New Shanghai Security Bureau Chief Yang Hu Takes Office 148

The position of Shanghai Security Bureau Chief, originally concurrently held by Mayor Wu, has now been filled by Yang Hu, recommended by Wu to the Military Affairs Commission for succession. Yang arrived at the Bureau at 9:00 AM yesterday to assume his duties. Over a hundred people including Huang Jinrong, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Wang Xiaolai, Yu Hongjun, Wu Xingya, Pan Gongzhan, Wen Hongen, Chen Yiting, Yin Dangeng, Yao Mulian, and Jin Liren, arrived one after another to offer congratulations.

Convocation and Admonition: After Yang Hu arrived, he immediately convened the staff and officers for admonition. First, Mayor Wu delivered an introductory speech. After the speech, Yang delivered a sincere admonition, roughly saying: "Fellow colleagues, I have been entrusted by the Mayor and have come here today to take office. Today is the first day I meet with you all. The Bureau has been established for only two or three months, and I have heard excellent feedback from all sectors. This is of course due to the leadership of Mayor Wu and the result of your collective efforts. My relationship with Mayor Wu is that, in public matters, we have worked together for a long time. In private, Mayor Wu and I have been friends in adversity for many years. Now we are serving together in the same place, under the guidance of the Mayor in the Security Bureau. Hereafter, I will handle matters in accordance with the methods originally established by Mayor Wu. I hope that you will continue to work hard for the Bureau as before. This is what I want to strive for together with you. We must all be loyal and responsible to our duties at the Bureau. Under the leadership of the Mayor, we must all work with vigor, and rewards and punishments must be clear, and merits and demerits must be clearly distinguished. I will be impartial and selfless in my duties toward all colleagues, without any perfunctoriness. All promotions, demotions, rewards, and punishments will be based entirely on performance evaluations. I hope you will all understand and pay attention to this. I will not say much today. In the future, we will often work together to shoulder the responsibilities of the Security Bureau."

Announcing Staff: After Yang Hu took office, he did not change any of the original staff. It is said that he did not want to easily transfer anyone and fall into the bad habits of officialdom, only announcing the appointments of Wu Huan as Director of the Office, Zou Yun as Chief of the Second Section, and Chen Qian as Secretary, among a few others.

Security Bureau Chief Yang Xiaotian

Yang Hu's Brief Biography: Yang's given name is Hu, courtesy name Xiaotian, from Ningguo County, Anhui Province. He has followed the Premier in the revolution for many years, serving as Military Counselor to the Grand Presidential Office, Military Counselor to the Grand Marshal's Office, Director of the Navy Department of the General Headquarters, and Commander of the First Division of the Northern Expeditionary Army. After 1926, he served as Director of the Special Affairs Department of the General Headquarters, Political Affairs Committee Member of the Anhui Provincial Government, Shanghai Garrison Commander, and Military Counselor to the National Government. River Pirates Rob Flowers in Suzhou Creek 150

Water Patrol in Disguise Captures Six

Whereabouts of Leader Wu Yusheng Unknown

The Xin Yi Public Insurance Company, and the Yongfu, Yutai, Shentai, and other flower clothing firms, jointly submitted a report to the Customs Water Patrol Police Station a few days ago, stating that water bandits frequently operate in the Suzhou Creek flower clothing firm area, specifically robbing flower clothing from ships. Each robbery results in losses of no less than several hundred yuan. With the new flowers entering the market, this is truly unbearable. They requested an investigation and capture, etc. The chief then ordered patrol officers to disguise themselves as boatmen the other night. When they reached the front of the Shenxin No. 1 Factory, a group of water bandits indeed drove a rowboat and attempted to rob the flower clothing. They were subsequently apprehended. Six individuals, Fang Shaowen, Zhang Yunxiang, Li Shengquan, Liu Kailin, Chang Qihua, and Shi Yu Yu, along with a rowboat, were taken to the police station. During interrogation, the suspects confessed that their leader was Wu Desheng, and their accomplices Cao Huisu, Lao Wu, Chen Little Monk, Little Sanzi, and Little Ma, etc., operated small goods stores in Caojiadu, etc., where they received stolen flowers. They bought them for twenty yuan a bundle and sold them for thirty-three yuan. If boatmen refused to sell, they would resort to robbery, etc. The suspects were deemed a major scourge of the Huangpu River. Therefore, they were prosecuted for robbery and handed over to the local court for investigation. They were transferred to the court yesterday for verification.

Business Community Dissatisfied with Meierhe's Remarks on the Issue of Reforming Customs Administration 152

Regarding the search of stores, Meierhe, the Inspector General of Customs, made a statement the other day to defend himself, which was recorded in yesterday's newspaper. A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency visited Mr. Zheng Chengqing, the representative of the petitioners, yesterday to ask for his opinion on Mr. Meierhe's remarks. Mr. Zheng replied as follows: Inspector General Meierhe made a statement in the local newspapers on the first of this month regarding the search of stores by the Jianghai Customs, the main points of which are: (1) It is not just Chinese stores that are being searched, and some foreign merchants have also been searched in the past. (2) Most of the goods seized by the Customs are directly imported from overseas and not purchased from foreign merchants, and there are often unscrupulous merchants colluding with foreign merchants to smuggle goods into China. These two points should be presented by the injured party when filing a petition, with the Customs providing concrete evidence to the competent authorities. Currently, these are just vague arguments, and we do not need to refute them. However, the main point of this case is whether the Customs' right to search can extend from the seaport to stores. This is the primary question. If this point is clarified, the rest is just rhetoric. According to Inspector General Meierhe, "The method of searching Chinese stores is also adopted by countries in the East and West, and the Jianghai Customs is not the first to create this precedent." These few words are enough to show that the Customs' current methods do not include the right to enter stores to search for Shanghai taxes. Therefore, he can only justify it by saying that it is also adopted by countries in the East and West. Comparing Inspector General Meierhe's statement with the Customs Administration's response to the petitioning representatives, it can be proved that the Customs' right to search is indeed limited to the seaport and its affiliated customs offices. We can calmly and objectively judge that the Customs handles tax collection as an agency for enforcing laws, not an agency for creating laws. Since the establishment of the Customs, the Inspector General has only had the right to propose suggestions for any matters that should be established or reformed. It must be approved and promulgated by the Prime Minister's Office or the Customs Administration's Tax Office or the Ministry of Finance before it can become a Customs regulation that applies throughout the country. When the government has not approved it, the precedents of countries in the East and West can only be the personal opinion of the Inspector General, submitted to the government for reference. Since the Customs has never had such a regulation for searching stores, if, as the Inspector General claims, it is necessary to do so, then this can be said to be "a new kind of power" that should be granted to the Customs by the central government before it can be implemented. The Customs cannot create laws or increase its own power. Therefore, according to the above argument, the Customs' extension of the right to suppress smuggling from the Customs to stores is at least responsible for (1) violating the law and (2) exceeding its authority. According to administrative regulations, this is enough to constitute grounds for disciplinary action. We hope that those who cherish the law will study this together.

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Scheduled to Inspect Imported Alcohol 154

Starting December 1st

Alcohol is widely needed for industrial and combustion purposes, but it is harmful to human health when used as a beverage. Therefore, various European and American countries have strict restrictions on the use of alcohol. All alcohol reported for combustion or industrial use must be mixed with toxic substances and clearly labeled in a prominent place on the packaging so that purchasers can see at a glance and dare not use it as a beverage. Our country has never had such regulations on alcohol, which is somewhat lacking in terms of protecting human health. In view of this, the Executive Yuan has promulgated regulations on the prohibition of alcohol, ordering the Ministry of Industry to instruct various commodity inspection bureaus to comply. The Ministry of Industry, based on the aforementioned regulations and the Provisional Regulations on Commodity Inspection, has formulated regulations on the inspection of imported alcohol, which have been submitted to the Executive Yuan for approval and promulgated by ministerial order. All imported alcohol will be subject to inspection starting December 1st of this year. Areas that already have commodity inspection bureaus will conduct inspections locally. Areas without inspection bureaus will import through nearby areas with inspection bureaus and then conduct inspections. Shanghai already has a commodity inspection bureau and should conduct inspections locally in accordance with the Ministry's regulations. Alcohol imported through Wuhu, Jiujiang, Nanjing, Zhenjiang, Suzhou, and Hangzhou will be imported through Shanghai and inspected by the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau. After receiving the order, the Bureau made preparations for inspection and decided to start processing on December 1st of this year. After December 1st, alcohol imported into Shanghai must be reported to the Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau for inspection in accordance with the regulations, and a certificate will be issued before it can be declared for import. Merchants who import alcohol or manufacture alcohol domestically and wish to know the regulations and details of the inspection can visit the Inspection Bureau after the 10th of this month to obtain them.

Anhui Public Groups Hold Joint Meeting Yesterday 157

Opposing the Provincial Government's Collection of Rice License Fees

The Anhui Association in Shanghai and the Anhui Student Association in Shanghai, due to the Anhui Provincial Government violating public opinion by establishing a Food Administration Bureau and collecting rice license fees, convened a joint meeting of all Anhui public groups in Shanghai at the Atlantic Western Restaurant on Sima Road at 3:00 PM yesterday.

Attending Representatives: Yesterday, over one hundred and ten people including Wang Shujiao, Li Cishan, Liu Zhuqing, Pan Ying, Fang Chen, Hu Peiru, Zhu Ziming, Lei Younan, Wang Zhuru, Li Shaochuan, Yu Kongwo, and Yuan Yeyu attended.

Chairman's Report: Li Cishan was elected as the chairman. After performing the rituals, the chairman first reported the purpose of the meeting, roughly saying: "This year, Anhui has had a bumper harvest, the first in twenty years. Farmers are generally suffering because the price of grain is too low, making their livelihoods extremely difficult. This situation is equivalent to a famine. Efforts should be made to circulate grain to create livelihoods for farmers. However, the provincial government has failed to observe the hardships of the people and has established a Food Administration Bureau to collect rice license fees, which is a disguised form of likin tax. Even during Chen Tiaoyuan's time, efforts were made to eliminate it. Now that the ruler is a native of Anhui, he is going against the tide. Therefore, we have convened a meeting of various groups to abolish this measure."

Resolutions: After the chairman's report, the proposals were discussed. (1) A proposal to send representatives to various ministries and departments in Beijing to petition. It was resolved to send representatives Hu Peiru, Liu Zhuqing, Zhu Zaixin, and Zhu Ziming to Beijing to petition. (2) A proposal to send representatives to the Hankou Headquarters to petition. It was resolved to pass it. (3) A proposal to send representatives to Anqing, Wuhu, Bengbu, and other places to appeal to all sectors for unified support. It was resolved to send six representatives to Anqing, Wuhu, and Bengbu. (4) A proposal to send a telegram to the provincial party headquarters to file an impeachment. It was resolved to pass it. (5) A proposal to create an iron statue of Chen Tiaoyuan, who caused the disaster in Anhui. It was resolved to hand it over to the two associations for design and implementation. (6) A proposal to send another telegram to the provincial government to quickly abolish the rice license fee. It was resolved to pass it. (7) It was heard that Jiang Wei was in charge of the Anhui Provincial Gazetteer Office, which has consumed huge sums of money over the years with no results. The association should send a letter to the provincial party and political organs to thoroughly investigate the matter. It was resolved to pass it. (8) A proposal to notify Anhui associations in various provinces and cities of the resolutions of the meeting. It was resolved to pass it.

New Standards for Shops Hanging Flags 160

Notice from the Nanjing Road Business Association to its Members

Thirteen Feet or Seven Feet Six Inches from the Ground

The Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council of the International Settlement sent a letter to the Nanjing Road Business Association, stating that many of the shop signs and advertising flags hanging in Nanjing Road violated Article 33 of the Police Regulations. They requested the Association to notify all shops to make reforms within two weeks, or they would be prosecuted according to the regulations. The Association felt that it would be difficult to make reforms according to the regulations, so they sent representatives to negotiate with the police department. A new compromise standard was reached. Therefore, yesterday, the Association notified all member shops, saying, "Regarding the notice, we have received a letter from the Chief Inspector of the Public Works Department stating that the flags hanging by shops are too low, violating Article 33 of the Police Regulations. Warnings have been issued, but most shops have not complied. If they do not comply within two weeks, the matter will be brought to court. This Association has been asked to advise them accordingly. We note that hanging flags is important for business, and it is not appropriate to remove them suddenly. However, the police authorities said that low-hanging flags obstruct the passage of police vehicles and fire engines (because these vehicles are taller than any other vehicles), and they also create obstacles for police officers performing their duties. In addition to replying to the police department that we would inform them, we also sent representatives to negotiate with the police department today. The result of the negotiation is that 'flags must be thirteen feet high from the road surface, and signs or awnings must be seven feet six inches (both in English feet) above the sidewalk.' We believe that all member businesses will prioritize public affairs and comply immediately."

Further Arrests in the Assassination of Zhao Xilin Case 162

Zhao's Concubine Witnessed the Shooting

Zhao Xilin, from Changzhou, was formerly a detective in the local Public Security Bureau, where he worked hard to arrest local thugs and bandits. After being dismissed, he came to Shanghai to work as an inspector at the Shenxin No. 9 Cotton Mill on Yangshupu Road. He had many enemies and was shot at three times. On the evening of June 13th of this year, at around 8:00 PM, he was shot and killed near Wanxingfang on Yangshupu Road. Shen Yuzhou, a Chinese detective from the Yangshupu Police Station, arrested Tang Fuchang, a suspect from Changzhou, and handed him over to the First Special District Court. After the interrogation was completed, he was awaiting sentencing. This has already been reported in this newspaper. The Changzhou natives, Fang Renzhao (also known as Fang Renchuan), Wu Zhiying (also known as Hou Rongchun), along with the suspect Tan Jinfu from Jiangwan, have been arrested and taken to the police station. Zhang Tianyin, a lawyer from the Criminal Division Three Police Station, stated yesterday that after investigation, the two defendants, Fang and Wu, were the main culprits in the third shooting of Zhao Xilin at Wanxingfang. Zhao's concubine, Jiang, identified them at the police station as the shooters. The defendant Wu Zhiying admitted that he shot Zhao Xilin at the time of the incident, and that the first shot was fired by Fang Renzhao, and the second shot was fired by him. Fang and Wu had committed several robbery cases in Changzhou, and the local authorities issued warrants for Zhao Xilin to arrest them, resulting in accumulated resentment. However, Fang denied being an accomplice at the police station, and the third defendant, Tan Jinfu, was detained for investigation. Judge Shen Bingrong granted Zhang's request and ordered the defendants to be interrogated separately. Jiang, the concubine of the victim Zhao Xilin, stated that she and her husband were coming from the Changzhou opera theater on Songpan Road and were walking near Wanxingfang when they suddenly heard gunshots from behind. When she turned around, she saw the two defendants, Fang and Wu, shooting nearby, about thirty to forty feet away. There was another person standing there, but she could not see his face clearly. Her husband was shot and fell to the ground. She wanted to chase after them, but her husband stopped her. She recognized the two defendants because they had previously visited the opera theater. Wu Zhiying confessed that his real name was Hou Rongchun, and that he was drinking tea at the Laohuzao on Songpan Road that night when he met Fang Renzhao. Fang asked him to help, and near Wanxingfang, Fang said that Zhao was coming, and he immediately shot. He did not act. The court said that he confessed in the police station that the second shot was fired by him, and there was no need to retract his confession. Wu then admitted that he also shot once, and afterwards, he and Fang fled together and stayed in a small inn near the Great World in the French Concession. The rest of his confession was evasive. He also claimed that he did not know Tan Jinfu and that he did not go there that night. Fang Renzhao confessed that he did not drink tea with Wu Zhiying in the Songpan Road and did not go to shoot Zhao. Tan Jinfu confessed that he knew Fang because they used to work together at the foreign-owned Samsung Cotton Mill, but he did not know Wu Zhiying and had nothing to do with the murder of Zhao Xilin. Judge Shen ordered all of them to be remanded in custody and investigated further.

The French Concession Municipal Council's Health Department issued a notice to residents of the concession: Starting this month, except for Saturday afternoons and Sundays, free smallpox vaccinations will be offered daily at the following three locations: (1) Clinic at No. 630 Beile Road; (2) Health Department Headquarters at No. 840 Xujiahui Road; (3) Mobile immunization vehicle within the concession. All employees of factories and public entertainment venues must be vaccinated according to regulations. Please come for vaccination immediately. This department can issue vaccination certificates. If these employees are unable to spare time due to work, please inform this department immediately, and a special team will be dispatched to provide vaccinations within the possible range.

Merger of Accounting Departments in the Second Special District Court 165

Since its establishment in August of last year, the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court in the French Concession and the Jiangsu Shanghai Second Special District Local Court have had independent accounting departments. Now, the Judicial Administration Department has instructed that the Third Branch of the High Court should handle the accounting matters of the subordinate local court, such as collecting litigation fees and selling legal documents. Liang Renjie, the President of the Third Branch of the High Court, upon receiving the order, immediately notified Ying Shi, the President of the Second Special District Court, to have all the accounting matters of the local court taken over by personnel dispatched from the Third Branch of the High Court starting from the first of this month (yesterday). A notice was issued, and President Ying, upon receiving the order, immediately instructed Wei Yuwei, the head of the Accounting Department of the Local Court, to expedite the handover. Starting yesterday, personnel dispatched from the Third Branch of the High Court have been stationed at the Local Court to manage all accounting matters.

Investigation into the Origin of Soviet Gold Banknotes 172

The police chief of the Lujiazui Branch of the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau's Huangpu River Water Patrol Team, along with police officers, intercepted Li Shunshai and Wang Yufu, two men from Yexian County, Shandong, on a barge. They were carrying thirty packages of new Soviet gold banknotes of varying amounts (each package containing 2,000-3,000), totaling 74,590 gold yuan, and nine musk pods. According to Li Shunshai and Wang Yufu, they had just arrived in China from Russia and produced a passport issued by the Chinese Consulate General in Vladivostok from the Ministry of Foreign Affairs. When asked about the origin of this huge amount of gold banknotes, they gave vague answers. The police, believing that the origin was unclear and suspecting that they might be providing aid to communists, detained Li Shunshai and Wang Yufu, along with the Russian gold banknotes, musk pods, and passports, and sent them to the headquarters for verification. After a brief interrogation by Captain Zhu, they were handed over to the General Bureau at 5:00 PM yesterday for further investigation.

Compilation of Bank Inspection Reports 176

Central Bank: The Central Bank's 141st inspection report on the issuance reserve states that, in accordance with Article 15 of the Central Bank Regulations, the bank is responsible for inspecting the reserve fund for the issuance of convertible banknotes. On October 31, 1932, Supervisor Qin Runqing conducted the 141st inspection at the bank's issuing branch and is announcing the results. (A) The total amount of convertible banknotes issued is 30,925,618 silver yuan, including 27,638,007 silver yuan banknotes and 3,287,611 subsidiary coin yuan. The total amount of the convertible banknote reserve fund is 30,925,618 yuan, including 25,111,618 yuan in cash reserve. This cash reserve includes 22,146,343.74 yuan in the bank's issuing treasury, 1,800,4297 yuan in branch banks in various ports, and 1,160,977.26 yuan deposited with other banks. The guarantee reserve is equivalent to 5,814,000 silver yuan. (B) The total amount of Customs Gold Unit convertible banknotes issued is 425,000 yuan. The total amount of the Customs Gold Unit convertible banknote reserve fund is 425,000 yuan, including 170,000 US dollars deposited with other banks in this city, converted to 425,000 Customs Gold Units at the fixed price of 40. According to Article 2 of the Central Bank's Convertible Banknote Regulations, the cash reserve is 60% and the protection reserve is 40%. The results of this inspection show that the cash exceeds 60% and the guarantee reserve is less than 40%, which is in accordance with the regulations. This is a special report. Board of Supervisors of the Central Bank, October 31, 1932.

China General Chamber of Commerce Bank: China General Chamber of Commerce Bank's report on the inspection of the issuance reserve states that the convertible banknotes and reserve fund issued by the China General Chamber of Commerce Bank in October have been inspected by supervisors Shao Ziyu, Yu Zuoting, Lu Shaotang, and Fu Qilin, together with accountant Xu Yongzuo, on November 1. The results of the inspection are listed below. (A) The amount of silver yuan convertible banknotes issued is 8,283,573 yuan, and the total amount of the reserve fund is 8,283,573 yuan, including 5,399,276 yuan in cash reserve (more than 60%) and 2,884,297 yuan in guarantee reserve (less than 40%). (B) The amount of silver tael convertible banknotes issued is 315,000 taels, and the total amount of the reserve fund is 315,000 taels in cash, which is in compliance with the issuance regulations.

Four Banks: The Four Banks Shanghai Reserve Depository report on the issuance reserve states that the Four Banks Reserve Depository is jointly established by the Yanyeh, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks to handle the issuance of banknotes by the Zhongnan Bank. According to the depository's issuance regulations, banknotes are issued with a 100% reserve, with a cash reserve of at least 60% and a guarantee reserve of at most 40%. It is announced once a week and is checked by the auditors and accountants of the Four Banks. The following is a record of the 148th announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Depository on October 29, 1932. The amount of banknotes in circulation is 23,087,757 yuan, and the total amount of the reserve fund is 23,087,757 yuan, including 14,189,247.87 yuan in cash reserve and 8,898,509.13 yuan in guarantee reserve.

Siming Bank: The Siming Bank's report on the inspection of the issuance reserve states that the bank issues banknotes with a 100% reserve, with a cash reserve of at least 60% and a guarantee reserve of at most 40%. The following is the report from accountants Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang and supervisors Xiang Fenglou and Zheng Xitang. The total amount of convertible banknotes issued is 11,596,400 yuan. The total amount of the reserve fund is 11,596,400 yuan, including 5,786,400 yuan issued by the bank, with 4,166,400 yuan in cash and 1,620,000 yuan in guarantee. The amount received is 5,810,000 yuan, with 3,590,000 yuan in cash and 2,220,000 yuan in guarantee. Accountants Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang and supervisors Xiang Fenglou and Zheng Xitang.

Letter 190

To the Editor,

Regarding the case reported by the Fifth District, it was found that on the 19th of this month (October), the police chief Li Xia of the Qujiaqiao Police Station reported that an unidentified male corpse, about 22 or 23 years old, was found behind the Central University on Jiangwan Road, wearing a navy blue serge student uniform and leather shoes, lying on the west side of the railway tracks. Before reporting, the local bailiff was ordered to go to the court for an examination, and telegrams were sent to the Supervision Department and a form was filled out to report to the department for verification. Subsequently, the court sent prosecutor Wu Deying to the scene to examine the corpse, and it was determined that the death was caused by injury. A burial notice No. 278 was filled out, and the Supervision Department sent Inspector Zhong Weiwu to the office to inspect the scene and report the notice to the bureau. It was found that the unidentified male corpse was rumored to have fallen from a train and died. However, the burial notice filled out by the prosecutor did not state the cause of death. In addition to taking photos of the corpse for record and ordering the local bailiff to bury it, it is appropriate to present a written report along with six photos for your examination and forwarding for public notice, so that the relatives of the deceased can come to claim the body. We would be grateful. To the Shenbao Newspaper Office. Enclosed is a photo. From the Shanghai Public Security Bureau, November 1st.

(8) The Committee may exercise the following powers and functions, which are delegated to the Committee in accordance with Section 28 of the Local Government Ordinance of 1926, without first seeking the approval of the Council:

A. Supervise and keep the accounts of the Council, manage the Municipal Finance Department, and control and manage the accounting section of each part of the Municipal Government.

B. Calculate and recover interest on overdue taxes and sanitation fees.

C. Exercise the powers conferred on the Council by Section 15 of the Local Tax Ordinance of 1928.

D. Make regulations from time to time to guide the various committees authorized to incur debt or use funds, as to how they should report to this Committee such debt or funds, whether they have been actually incurred or used, or are intended to be incurred or used.

E. Prepare funds for annual purchase of goods and audit the accounts of various items.

F. Obtain bonds from officers entrusted with the custody of money on behalf of the Council, or amend existing bonds from time to time as necessary.

G. Dispose of and manage any retirement savings, reserves, or other funds of a similar nature intended to benefit the members of the Council.

H. General financial control of the various works carried out by the Council.

I. Manage all goods and all purchases necessary for the Council, prepare purchase plans, consider tenders for the supply of various goods to the Council in accordance with the reports of the relevant specialized committees, and dispose of surplus materials, machinery, and livestock.

2. General Affairs Committee

In addition to the chairmen of the other standing committees and ex-officio members, this Committee shall consist of four additional members appointed by the Council. If the chairman of any standing committee is absent on leave, the acting chairman of that committee shall represent him/her on the Committee. The powers of this Committee are as follows:

(1) To consider, and if necessary, report on how the Council and any committee or part thereof conducts its administrative work, and to make such recommendations regarding the conduct of such work as it deems fit.

(2) Manage the Municipal Secretariat.

(3) To consider and report on all matters relating to the appointment and dismissal of heads of departments and staff of the Municipal Secretariat. The heads of departments referred to are the Municipal Secretary, Health Officer, Head of the Finance Department, Municipal Engineer, General Manager of the Electricity Department, Head of the Fire Brigade, Superintendent of Slaughterhouses and Livestock Markets, Superintendent of Transport and Cleaning, and General Manager of the Tramway Department.

(4) To consider and report on the accommodation facilities of the various Municipal Government offices and any new facilities required in the future.

(5) To review in detail the agenda before it is submitted to the Council.

(6) To consider, and if necessary, report on the following matters:

A. Any regulations made or proposed that affect the Council.

B. Council Rules, Financial Regulations, and Leave Regulations.

C. The terms of reference of the Committees.

(7) To consider and report on any matters not submitted to any other Committee.

(8) Any new proposal which this Committee considers to be sufficiently important may be specified by this Committee as to its relationship to the Constitution, the Council's usual standards of practice, or any other work it has undertaken or proposes to undertake.

(9) The Committee may exercise the following powers and functions, which are delegated to the Committee in accordance with Section 28 of the Local Government Ordinance of 1926, without first seeking the approval of the Council:

A. On behalf of the Council, to implement and enforce all by-laws relating to the licensing of theatres, music halls, public halls, concert halls, and other places of public entertainment and banquets.

B. On behalf of the Council, to implement and enforce any Council by-laws relating to matters not submitted to any other Committee.

C. On behalf of the Council, to supervise any public bodies under the control of the Council but not within the purview of any other Committee.

D. On behalf of the Council, to supervise the Council's investigation into the population of Johannesburg.

E. Supervise the preparation of the municipal electoral roll and deal with registration petitions.

F. Supervise the construction and maintenance of all works relating to the matters within the purview of this Committee.

G. The Committee may decide on behalf of the Council whether or not to grant licenses for all occupations not listed under the Public Health By-laws, as required by the Regulations for the Suppression of and Trade in Opium of 1926, or any amendments thereto.

H. The Committee may decide whether or not to grant any license required within the scope of this Committee in accordance with the By-laws, but this shall not apply to cases where the Council may, in accordance with the By-laws, organize a special court to deal with the By-laws concerning theatres, music halls, public halls, concert halls, and other places of public entertainment and banquets.

3. Health Committee

This Committee shall consist of seven members, in addition to the ex-officio Committee members.

The powers of this Committee are as follows:

(1) Manage the Health Department, the Transport and Cleaning Department, and the Slaughterhouse and Livestock Market Management Department. The Committee shall consider and report on all matters relating to the appointment and dismissal of staff in each of these departments, except for the Medical Officer of Health, the Superintendent of Transport and Cleaning, and the Superintendent of Slaughterhouses and Livestock Markets.

(2) To consider and report on all matters relating to slaughterhouses and cattle and sheep exchanges (municipal or non-municipal) and, on behalf of the Council, to supervise the management of any such undertaking now or hereafter under the jurisdiction of the Council.

(3) To consider and report on all matters relating to hospitals and asylums and, on behalf of the Council, to supervise the management of all such institutions under the jurisdiction of the Council.

(4) To consider, and if necessary, report on all matters relating to the disposal of sewer water.

(5) To consider, and if necessary, report on any plans for the collection, removal, and disposal of feces, sewage, bath water, refuse, and other waste.

(6) To consider and report on all questions relating to the levying of any funds, taxes, or payment of expenses required to conduct any business within the scope of this Committee.

(7) The Committee may exercise the following powers and functions, which are delegated to the Committee in accordance with Section 28 of the Local Government Ordinance of 1926, without first seeking the approval of the Council:

(1) To implement and enforce all by-laws relating to washing and laundry work.

(2) To implement and enforce the Council's by-laws relating to the suppression of the following: teahouses, coffee shops, restaurants, eateries, boarding houses, milk parlors, milk vending shops, cowsheds, cake shops, butcher shops, slaughterhouses, barbers, hairdressers, barber shops and hairdressing salons, and all factories or places for the preparation of food or beverages for sale or use.

(3) To manage and supervise all matters relating to the public health and sanitation of the city and the removal of all nuisances in the city, and on behalf of the Council, to implement and enforce all by-laws relating to such matters.

(4) To supervise the collection and removal of dust, ashes, feces, sewage, and sludge, and on behalf of the Council, to implement and enforce all by-laws relating to such collection.

(5) To implement and enforce all by-laws relating to the closure of all or part of dwellings inhabited by transient people.

(6) To implement and enforce all by-laws relating to the prevention of infectious diseases, and to take all necessary measures regarding cleaning, fumigation, and disinfection.

(7) To implement and enforce all by-laws to keep the water supply or reservoirs clean, whether such water supply or reservoirs are located inside or outside the city.

(8) To implement and enforce all by-laws relating to the slaughter of cattle, sheep, and other animals, and the sale of meat. Also, to implement and enforce all by-laws relating to diseased animals, meat or food or beverages unfit for human consumption, and any food or beverage that has been adulterated or reduced in its proper standard or quality.

(9) To supervise the management of all public convenience businesses under the control of the Council. (To be continued)

Shanghai Shenbao Supplement

Commentary

Talking about Liang Zuoyou Again 192

— Buddha

Liang Zuoyou donated 30 million yuan. I have discussed this several times. Now, talking about Liang Zuoyou again might be annoying. But I dare not talk about people with higher status than Liang Zuoyou. And there's no need to talk about people less worthy than Liang Zuoyou. So, I can only talk about Liang Zuoyou again.

When the news of Liang Zuoyou's donation of 30 million yuan first spread, I was very skeptical. I thought it was a false story. Now it has become clear that it was indeed a deceptive act. According to news from Beijing yesterday, Liang Zuoyou, who claimed to donate funds to save the country, failed in his plan and was exposed. Ashamed to face people, he returned to his hometown of Huang County, Shandong Province, with his entourage on the Jinpu Railway the day before yesterday. The farce of donating huge sums of money that shocked the country has finally come to an end.

But Liang Zuoyou went to Beijing with his entourage to petition, destroy his family to save the country, and donate huge sums of money. In reality, it was a "empty city strategy." Anyone with common sense would know that this kind of trick would not work. But Liang Zuoyou shamelessly visited officials and deceived the people. His plan and actions showed that he was not mentally ill. He would not have dared to be so bold and reckless, speaking nonsense. It seems that he should be ignored and not discussed.

However, Liang has been in Beijing for a long time, and his attitude is calm, and his words are ambiguous. He does not seem to be mentally ill. And the result is completely deceptive. Not a penny has been paid. Not only have the people been deceived, but the government has also been tricked. Such a cunning person should be punished by the government to warn against such trickery.
